    A hand-out picture taken in the 60s and released on November 18, 2014 by the Institut des Hautes Etudes Scientifiques (IHES - Institute of Advanced Scientific Studies) shows German-born French mathematician Alexander Grothendieck (L) speaking with French mathematician Laurent Schwartz (R) in Bure-sur-Yvette, southwestern France. Alexander Grothendieck, one of the great eccentric geniuses of 20th century mathematics, has died in France at the age of 86 on November 14, 2014. The maths master reached the very pinnacle of his profession before abandoning the discipline, taking up anti-war activism, retreating into the life of a recluse and refusing to share his research. Grothendieck went on to become a revolutionary mathematician, doing groundbreaking work on algebra and geometry that won him the Fields medal, known as the Nobel prize of the maths world, in 1966.
